<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Query acceleration will be available for an early access preview in the next few weeks. You can learn more by watching the Microsoft Build on-demand session “<a href="https://aka.ms/OD813"></a><a href="https://aka.ms/OD813" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">OD813 &#8211; Powering modern data analytics in Fabric Data Warehouse</a>.”</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="curating-semantic-meaning">3. Curating semantic meaning with Fabric IQ, now generally available</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Once data is prepared, the next challenge is not access but understanding. Most organizations lack a shared layer of business context, forcing every agent to relearn how the business works from fragmented data. Fabric IQ, now generally available, addresses this gap.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">With data unified in OneLake, Power BI’s industry-leading semantic models then provide structured representations of your data for trusted business intelligence, serving as an ideal foundation for training agents. </p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Ontologies in Fabric IQ, expected to be generally available in the coming months, extend semantic models by adding operational context. They define business entities, relationships, properties, rules, and actions, and connect to live signals from Fabric Real-Time Intelligence. Operations agents, now generally available, then reason over shared live context, make decisions based on policy, and take action in the moment. Running on the governed foundation of Fabric and integrated with Microsoft Foundry, operations agents move beyond answering questions to driving action and outcomes.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="800" height="450" src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/06/OntologiesBuild2026MP4V3.gif" alt="GIF of entities, relationships, properties, actions and business objectives all being created based on products, inventory, stores, shipments, buyers, and suppliers" class="wp-image-51409" /></figure>



<h4 class="wp-block-heading" id="announcing-the-general-availability-of-graph-and-planning-in-fabric-1">Announcing the general availability of graph and planning in Fabric</h4>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We’re announcing the general availability of graph in Fabric, with general availability of the planning in Fabric coming later this month. Available today, graph introduces a highly scalable, relationship‑first model that connects business entities, systems, and signals so teams and agents can understand how changes propagate across the enterprise and act with full context. Planning extends this foundation by enabling organizations to create plans, budgets, forecasts, and scenario models on top of Fabric’s semantic models. Notably, planning in Fabric is not just static outputs. They can be written back into Fabric to drive execution, enabling closed-loop alignment with the same system of data and context.</p>



<h4 class="wp-block-heading" id="extending-fabric-iq-to-microsoft-foundry-and-agent-365">Extending Fabric IQ to Microsoft Foundry and Agent 365</h4>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Today, we are extending Fabric IQ across the agent ecosystem so this shared understanding can be used consistently across every agent and application. </p>



<h5 class="wp-block-heading" id="microsoft-foundry-and-agent-365"><strong>Microsoft Foundry and Agent 365&nbsp;</strong></h5>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Now in preview, Ontologies are accessible directly from Microsoft Foundry as knowledge sources, bringing trusted business context into both custom and built-in agent experiences. Also in preview, Fabric IQ is now integrated with Microsoft Agent 365 as a first-party model context protocol (MCP) tool, enabling organizations to ground agents in shared meaning and ensure consistent behavior across their agent estate.</p>



<h5 class="wp-block-heading" id="microsoft-foundry-and-agent-365"><strong><strong>Microsoft 365 Copilot: Cowork and Copilot Chat</strong>&nbsp;</strong></h5>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Fabric IQ is also extending into Microsoft 365 Copilot, including Cowork and Copilot Chat. This enables agents to access governed Fabric data, starting with Power BI reports and semantic models, to turn insights into action. Instead of static dashboards, agents can detect changes in key metrics, generate updates, trigger follow-ups, and schedule next steps, all grounded in trusted, governed data. The result is faster, more consistent execution across the organization. These experiences are currently available customers in Frontier with a Microsoft 365 Copilot license. <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365-copilot/frontier-individuals?msockid=053354d6877e66602b7b41a286ec67a0">Join the program today</a>.</p>



<h5 class="wp-block-heading" id="microsoft-foundry-and-agent-365"><strong><strong><strong>GitHub Copilot CLI</strong>&nbsp;</strong></strong></h5>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Using <a href="https://github.com/microsoft/skills-for-fabric" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Agent Skills for Fabric</a>, Fabric IQ tools and skills for data insights are accessible through GitHub Copilot CLI, bringing governed semantic context directly into the terminal. Now you can also query Power BI reports and semantic models from the command line, grounded in governed semantic context in Fabric IQ. Teams can ask natural language questions about usage, metrics, or customer behavior and get answers grounded in Fabric data directly within their workflow, reducing back-and-forth and accelerating data-driven decisions.&nbsp;</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Learn more about these enhancements in the Build on‑demand session “<a href="https://aka.ms/OD812"></a><a href="https://aka.ms/OD812" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">OD812 &#8211;&nbsp;Bringing Enterprise Ontology Directly into the Developer Workflow</a>.”</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="empowering-agents">4. Empowering agents to act with operations agents and Copilot in Fabric</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Enterprises are increasingly moving to multi-agent systems made up of specialized agents grounded in specific data or domain expertise. These agents can be reused across multiple systems, making it easier to scale and deliver more consistent outcomes.</p>



<h4 class="wp-block-heading" id="announcing-the-general-availability-of-operations-agents">Announcing the general availability of operations agents</h4>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Microsoft Fabric supports this shift with native agent capabilities, including Fabric data agents and operations agents. I’m excited to share operations agents are now generally available. These agents are designed to continuously monitor real-time data, detect patterns or anomalies, and act based on predefined business logic.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-bloginabox-theme-ump-embed wp-block-msx-ump-embed" class="wp-block-bloginabox-theme-ump-embed">
	<div class="wp-block-embed__wrapper">

<h4 class="wp-block-heading" id="apply-agentic-analytics-in-power-bi">Apply agentic analytics in Power BI</h4>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">In addition, we recently released open-source <a href="https://github.com/microsoft/skills-for-fabric">Agent Skills for Fabric</a>, designed to make it easier for AI tools and agents to interact directly with Fabric. These capabilities now extend to Power BI, enabling developers and analysts to create reports using natural language or even a screenshot of the desired outcome, significantly accelerating how insights are built and shared.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Copilot in Power BI can now also modify semantic models, with built-in recommendations that improve performance and make models more AI-ready. This helps teams iterate faster and deliver insights more quickly without leaving the tools they already use.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Learn more by reading the&nbsp;<a href="https://aka.ms/PowerBI-Build26" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Power BI blog</a>&nbsp;or by watching the Microsoft Build on-demand session “<a href="https://aka.ms/OD817"></a><a href="https://aka.ms/OD817" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">OD817 &#8211;&nbsp;Agentic analytics with Power BI and Microsoft Fabric</a>.&#8221;</p>

<p class="wp-block-paragraph">As organizations increasingly embrace the agentic era for AI, customer demands for compute are reshaping the architecture of cloud infrastructure as we know it. Today at <strong>Microsoft Build 2026, we are announcing the early access preview for <a href="https://aka.ms/Cobalt200VMs-signup" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure Cobalt 200 Arm-based Virtual Machines</a> (VMs)</strong>, designed from the ground up for scale-out, cloud-native, and Linux-based agentic AI workloads, with up to 50% better generational performance over Cobalt 100.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Cobalt 200 is purpose-built from silicon to servers to services—integrating Microsoft&#8217;s latest innovations in security, networking, storage, and offload to outperform traditional Arm-based compute. That hardware-software co-optimization lets us push the boundaries of scale, security, and cost for AI inferencing, data pipelines, and the web and API tiers that power modern services. Agents are unique from traditional workloads: they reason, make sequential decisions, and run continuously at scale—demanding a fundamentally different computational profile. Cobalt 200 is built for exactly this environment, delivering 50% performance gains for the workloads defining the next era of enterprise AI, making agents faster, more capable, and economically viable at scale.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://aka.ms/Cobalt200VMs-signup" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><strong>Get early access to Azure Cobalt 200 VMs</strong></a></div>
</div>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="building-on-the-success-of-cobalt-100-vms">Building on the success of Cobalt 100 VMs</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Microsoft Azure Cobalt 100, our first custom-built processor for cloud-native workloads is now deployed in 32 Azure datacenter regions around the world, with cloud analytics leaders like Databricks and Snowflake adopting Cobalt 100 to optimize their cloud footprint, while customers like Amadeus, OneTrust, Siemens, Sprinklr, and Temenos have achieved significant real-world performance and efficiency gains.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Within Microsoft’s own cloud services, Azure Cobalt 100 VMs are delivering up to 45% better performance while using 35% fewer compute cores compared to its previous compute platform. <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-in/security/business/endpoint-security/microsoft-defender-endpoint" id="https://www.microsoft.com/en-in/security/business/endpoint-security/microsoft-defender-endpoint" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft Defender for Endpoint (MDE)</a> saw 40% better performance in its cyber data curator, enabling faster threat response at massive scale.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">With Cobalt 200 VMs, we are applying everything we learned towards supporting these demanding services to raise the bar even further.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="what-s-new-in-cobalt-200-arm-based-vms">What’s new in Cobalt 200 Arm-based VMs</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The <a href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/azureinfrastructureblog/announcing-cobalt-200-azure%E2%80%99s-next-cloud-native-cpu/4469807">Cobalt 200 CPU represents a significant leap forward in performance, security, and efficiency</a>. At the heart of every Cobalt 200 VM is the Cobalt 200 System-on-Chip (SoC), our second-generation Arm processor built around the Arm Neoverse V3 Compute Subsystems, the highest-performance V-series core in Arm’s portfolio. Fabricated on TSMC’s 3nm (N3P) process, Cobalt 200 features a modern chiplet architecture, custom accelerators, and a custom memory controller.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Key innovations in Cobalt 200 VMs include:</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Generational performance gains across compute, storage, and networking: </strong>Compared to previous-generation Cobalt 100 VMs, new Cobalt 200 VMs deliver up to 50% better CPU performance, 20% higher remote storage IOPS with NVMe, 10% better remote storage throughput with NVMe, and 15% higher network bandwidth, with improvements varying by workload. </li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Up to 128 vCPUs: </strong>Cobalt 200 VMs scale up to 128 vCPUs, delivering more compute capacity for demanding scale-out, cloud-native, agentic AI, and data-intensive workloads. </li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Faster remote storage and networking: </strong><a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/virtual-machines/boost" id="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/virtual-machines/boost" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure Boost</a> integration helps improve remote storage IOPS and throughput with NVMe while increasing network bandwidth, benefiting distributed applications, storage-intensive services, and high-throughput data pipelines. </li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Advanced cache and scalable system design: </strong>A modern chiplet architecture with a larger cache hierarchy—including 3 MB of L2 cache per core and 192 MB of system-level L3 cache—keeps more active data closer to the workload, helping reduce latency and improve responsiveness for databases, in-memory caches, analytics engines, and other data-intensive services. </li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Stronger security by default: </strong>Memory encryption is enabled by default through a custom-designed memory controller, helping raise the baseline security posture for every workload with negligible performance impact. </li>
</ul>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="performance-for-agentic-ai-workloads">Performance for agentic AI workloads</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Cobalt 200 delivers the per-core performance and scalability needed to power modern agentic AI workloads. Each Cobalt 200 core is a full physical core, paired with dedicated 3 MB of L2 cache, and leading memory bandwidth per core. These design points enable higher isolation and sustained performance under load, which allow agentic workloads to pack more agent sandboxes per VM while meeting latency and throughput requirements.</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="real-cloud-workload-performance">Real cloud workload performance</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Cobalt 200 VMs show a broad generational uplift over Cobalt 100 on the workloads that matter most in production.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">With cloud workloads, we observe:</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Up to 135% better performance for cloud database workloads.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Up to 40% better performance for web serving workloads.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Up to 45% better performance for communication encryption workloads.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">And up to 80% better performance for caching workloads.</li>
</ul>


<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a3b521f329dc&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a3b521f329dc" class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full wp-lightbox-container"><img decoding="async" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/06/Screenshot-2026-06-01-163310.webp" alt="Cobalt 200 bar chart, per v C P U performance increase relative to Cobalt 100." class="wp-image-51459 webp-format" srcset="" data-orig-src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/06/Screenshot-2026-06-01-163310.webp"><button

<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The uplift measured is visible in real hyperscale services. Taken together, these results show that Cobalt 200 raises the floor on per-core performance across cloud-native applications, databases, analytics, caches, and communications workloads.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="industry-partners-and-customer-adoption">Industry partners and customer adoption</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We have been working closely with our technology partners and customers during the preview period to ensure Cobalt 200 Arm-based VMs deliver strong results across a wide range of real-world workloads. Leading software development companies and enterprises are already evaluating and adopting these VMs for their most demanding applications.</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="teradata">Teradata</h3>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow has-quote-default-font-size">
<p class="has-large-font-size wp-block-paragraph">Teradata is excited to be an early preview partner for Microsoft’s Cobalt 200 VMs. Microsoft has been a strong partner, and we value the opportunity to help shape the design and specifications to better meet the needs of our joint customers. Early testing has been encouraging, and we look forward to continued collaboration.</p>
<cite>—Brandon Mincey, Engineering Fellow, Teradata</cite></blockquote>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="elastic">Elastic</h3>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow has-quote-default-font-size">
<p class="has-large-font-size wp-block-paragraph">Elastic is committed to delivering best-in-class performance with the Search AI Platform that powers observability, security, search, and AI solutions. Performance and cost efficiency are critical for teams running these workloads at scale and our initial testing of the new Cobalt 200 VMs shows promise for further improvements in these areas. We look forward to bringing these benefits to Elasticsearch users on Azure through our continued collaboration with Microsoft.</p>
<cite>—Yuvraj Gupta, Director, Product Management, Elastic</cite></blockquote>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="arm">Arm</h3>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow has-quote-default-font-size">
<p class="has-large-font-size wp-block-paragraph">Agentic AI is reshaping the cloud and creating demand for infrastructure that can efficiently orchestrate and scale millions of intelligent interactions in real time. Our collaboration with Microsoft on Cobalt 200, built on Arm Neoverse CSS V3, reflects how purpose-built Arm-based compute is enabling the next generation of AI-driven services while continuing to deliver exceptional performance for cloud-native applications.</p>
<cite>—Eddie Ramirez, Vice President of go-to-market, Cloud AI Business Unit, Arm</cite></blockquote>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="canonical">Canonical</h3>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow has-quote-default-font-size">
<p class="has-large-font-size wp-block-paragraph">Cobalt 200 delivers key advances for production Linux workloads on Arm, including memory encryption enabled by default, built-in acceleration for compression and encryption, and higher throughput for data-intensive cloud services. Ubuntu gives organizations a consistent platform for cloud-native and agentic AI workloads across Azure, and Ubuntu Pro keeps it production-ready with long-term security maintenance and Livepatch, which now brings rebootless kernel updates to Arm so always-on services stay available.</p>
<cite>—Jehudi Castro-Sierra, Public Cloud Alliance Director, Canonical</cite></blockquote>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="developer-ecosystem-and-arm-compatibility">Developer ecosystem and Arm compatibility</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The Arm developer ecosystem continues to thrive. Cobalt 200 Arm-based VMs deliver full compatibility for workloads currently running on Cobalt 100 VMs, making migration seamless. Major developer platforms and languages—including C++, .NET, Java, Python, and Rust—provide Arm-native versions with optimizations that fully leverage the capabilities of the Arm architecture.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The broader ecosystem has embraced Arm with native support across popular infrastructure and deployment solutions. GitHub Actions supports Arm through both self-hosted and GitHub-hosted runners. <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/kubernetes-service" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure Kubernetes Service (AKS)</a> supports Arm agent nodes as well as mixed x86 and Arm architecture clusters. Containerized workloads benefit from the growing availability of Arm-native container images across the ecosystem.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="microsoft-services-powered-by-cobalt-200-vms">Microsoft services powered by Cobalt 200 VMs</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Microsoft’s own cloud services are among the first to adopt Cobalt 200 Arm-based VMs, building on the success of Cobalt 100 adoption across our most demanding, mission-critical workloads.</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="dataverse">Dataverse</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Dataverse is the core application and data platform underpinning Dynamics and Power Platform workloads, requiring high performance, scalability, and low latency to deliver a responsive customer experience.</p>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow has-quote-default-font-size">
<p class="has-large-font-size wp-block-paragraph">We deployed the Power Apps platform on Cobalt 100 for its improved performance and power efficiency. We are validating Cobalt 200 now and excited by the performance gains we are seeing&#8211;up to 60% better performance for our base workload over Cobalt 100.</p>
<cite>—Mauktik Gandhi, VP Engineering, Agent 365 Platform</cite></blockquote>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="azure-databases">Azure Databases</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/azure-sql/database" id="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/azure-sql/database" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure SQL Database</a> is a natural fit for Cobalt 200 Arm-based VMs. The built-in compression and cryptography accelerators are particularly impactful for database workloads—by offloading compression and encryption tasks to the Cobalt 200 accelerator, Azure SQL is able to reduce the use of critical compute resources, prioritizing them for customer queries and transactions.</p>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow has-quote-default-font-size">
<p class="has-large-font-size wp-block-paragraph">Our teams collaborated from the beginning to ensure that the architecture of Cobalt 200 is optimized for hosting databases in Azure. We are excited about the performance gains we are seeing over Cobalt 100 and looking forward to broader availability later this year.</p>
<cite>—Shireesh Thota, Corporate Vice President, Azure Databases</cite></blockquote>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="vm-families-and-specifications">VM families and specifications</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Cobalt 200 VMs significantly expand our Arm VM portfolio based on customer feedback to support a broader set of workloads. While Cobalt 100 offered General Purpose (Dp,Dpl), and Memory Optimized (Ep) VM families, Cobalt 200 adds two more VM families: the High-Memory Optimized Mpsv4 VMs and Dense Local Storage Lpsv5 VMs, bringing more choice across compute, memory, and storage profiles.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">All VM series deliver up to 85 Gbps of network bandwidth and 70 Gbps of remote storage throughput, except Mpsv4/Mpdsv4, which provide up to 70 Gbps of network bandwidth and 46 Gbps of remote storage throughput. Most series are available with or without local NVMe disks, while Lpsv5 includes local NVMe storage across all sizes, giving customers flexibility to optimize for cost or performance.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-table is-style-regular"><table><thead><tr><th class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">VM family</th><th class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">vCPUs</th><th <br><strong>Lpsv5</strong> </td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">1–128</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">8:1</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Yes – Up to 23 TB</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left"><p>Data pre-processing and staging, relational and NoSQL databases with local storage requirements, big data analytics, and search/index engines.</p></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">All Cobalt 200 VMs will support remote disk types including Standard SSD, Standard HDD, Premium SSD, and Ultra Disk storage. You can deploy these new VMs using existing methods, including the Azure portal, SDKs, APIs, PowerShell, and the command-line interface (CLI).</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="availability">Availability</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Cobalt 200 Arm-based VMs are now available in preview. The new VMs will be available in preview in the following regions: West US3, East US2, Central US, Sweden Central, East US, West US2, Spain Central, and Indonesia Central, with additional regions to be announced.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="the-next-chapter-in-azure-s-custom-silicon-journey">The next chapter in Azure’s custom silicon journey</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The announcement of Cobalt 200 Arm-based Virtual Machines marks the next chapter in Azure’s purpose-built infrastructure journey. With our end-to-end systems approach—designing the CPU in-house and optimizing it for Azure’s infrastructure—we are delivering a tightly integrated platform that offers performance, power efficiency, and security for our customers.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Whether you’re accelerating product development, scaling analytics platforms, running mission-critical databases, or improving user experiences, Cobalt 200 Arm-based VMs offer a compelling choice for modern cloud workloads. We are excited to see how our customers and partners create breakthrough products and services on this new platform.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Try the Cobalt 200 Arm-based VMs today in early access preview and experience the next generation of Azure’s custom infrastructure innovation.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Thank you for joining us on this exciting journey.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Get <a href="https://aka.ms/Cobalt200VMs-signup" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">early access to Azure Cobalt 200 VMs</a>.</p>

		<title>Foundry IQ: Build smarter agents faster with unified knowledge and serverless retrieval</title>
		<link>https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/build-smarter-agents-faster-with-foundry-iq/</link>
					<comments>https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/build-smarter-agents-faster-with-foundry-iq/#respond</comments>
		
		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Pablo Castro]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Tue, 02 Jun 2026 16:00:00 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[AI + machine learning]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[AI]]></category>
		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/?p=51599</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>Build smarter agents with Microsoft Foundry IQ, unifying enterprise and external data into a secure, scalable knowledge layer for faster, higher-quality answers.</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/build-smarter-agents-faster-with-foundry-iq/">Foundry IQ: Build smarter agents faster with unified knowledge and serverless retrieval</a> appeared first on <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog">Microsoft Azure Blog</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[
<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Developers building agent fleets keep hitting the same pattern: the agent logic is ready, but the knowledge infrastructure underneath is complex to do well. Getting to production means solving for stability, scale, data access, answer quality, security, and content ingestion all at once. Today, we are enabling developers to have faster impact by simplifying the enterprise knowledge platform.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Your company’s IQ,&nbsp;<a href="http://aka.ms/iq" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">powered by Microsoft IQ</a>, is the collective intelligence locked in documents, emails, meetings, operational data, and the live web. This is where your true competitive edge lives. Foundry IQ grounds agents with the knowledge from these sources and continuously improves based on your business goals.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The announcements today are designed to help customers provision knowledge bases faster, unify enterprise and external sources, and expose that knowledge through the Foundry IQ Model Context Protocol (MCP) server for any agent framework or MCP-compatible hosts.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="what’s-new">What’s new</h2>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Foundry IQ Serverless in preview:</strong> Provision instant, no-friction context retrieval with scale to zero pricing. Developer tier now available in public preview with more coming soon. <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/search/search-sku-tier" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Docs</a> | <a href="https://ai.azure.com/nextgen/goto/build/knowledge" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Create a Foundry IQ resource</a></li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>New knowledge sources in preview:</strong> Ground agents across Work IQ, Fabric IQ (including Data agents and Ontology), File Search, Azure SQL, and MCP through a multi-source knowledge base, with no custom integrations required. <a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-new" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Docs</a> | <a href="https://microsoft-foundry.github.io/forgebook/notebook/mastering-foundry-iq/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Cookbook</a></li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Web IQ in Foundry IQ is now available:</strong> Extend agent context to the web, honoring publisher preferences, and marketplace data with sub-165 ms latency and zero data retention. <a href="https://aka.ms/nextgengrounding" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://aka.ms/webiq" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Website</a></li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Foundry IQ knowledge bases are generally available:</strong> Ship production agents on a fully SLA-backed knowledge layer with stable APIs, compliance certifications, and the Foundry IQ MCP server for any MCP-compatible host. <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/foundry/agents/how-to/foundry-iq-connect?tabs=foundry%2Cpython" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Docs</a> | <a href="https://microsoft-foundry.github.io/forgebook/notebook/mastering-foundry-iq/#20-talk-to-the-knowledge-base-directly-over-mcp" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Quickstart</a></li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Agentic retrieval quality improvements:</strong> The latest updates to the agentic retrieval engine improve answer performance across datasets, effort tiers, and model sizes while spending fewer tokens. <a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-evals" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/search/search-get-started-agentic-retrieval?tabs=windows&amp;pivots=csharp" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Quickstart</a></li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Data pipeline updates in preview:</strong> Automatic layout-aware ingestion of documents, image enrichment, and broader SharePoint indexing ground agents in complete documents, not just raw text. <a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-data" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-data-samples" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Quickstart</a></li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Security updates in preview:</strong> New controls for encryption, permissions sync, and sensitivity-label governance keep enterprise policy intact as content flows into agents. <a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-security" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://github.com/Azure-Samples/azure-search-openai-demo-purviewdatasecurity" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Quickstart</a></li>
</ul>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="foundry-iq-serverless-in-public-preview">Foundry IQ Serverless in public preview</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We know agent workloads are bursty and event-driven: an agent might execute hundreds of steps in seconds, then go idle for hours. Serverless eliminates infrastructure friction: no clusters to manage, no capacity to reserve, no idle costs. Go from zero to production fast, with instant retrieval-augmented generation (RAG) and state-of-the-art retrieval quality built in.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Foundry IQ Serverless (Developer tier) is available in public preview. You are billed for compute resources and storage used, and the service scales to zero when idle.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Serverless tiers use Compute Units (CU) to measure resource consumption, including CPU utilization, memory and storage I/O. Usage is calculated each minute in increments of 0.25 CUs.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For large-scale serverless deployments,&nbsp;<a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-serverless-contact" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">contact us</a>&nbsp;for additional options.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-fixed-layout"><thead><tr><th class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Capability</th><th class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Developer tier</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Compute usage</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">$0.24 CU / hour</td></tr><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Indexed storage</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Up to $0.29 GB / month; GB cost is region dependent</td></tr><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Indexed storage per index</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">1 GB / index</td></tr><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Indexes per service</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">30 indexes / service</td></tr><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Services per subscription per region</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">5 services / subscription / region</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><em>Billing is expected to begin in late 2026 with details provided at least 30 days in advance. Customers using Serverless Developer won’t be charged before billing is enabled. Current Compute Unit measurements are estimates only and subject to change before billing is enabled.</em></p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Next steps:&nbsp;<a href="https://ai.azure.com/nextgen/goto/build/knowledge" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">create a Foundry IQ Serverless resource</a>&nbsp;in the Foundry portal.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="new-knowledge-sources-in-preview">New knowledge sources in preview</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><em>How do I give an agent access to organizational knowledge and structured business data without building a custom connector for every system?</em></p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Bringing enterprise knowledge into agent workflows often means stitching together custom integrations across each data source. Developers must account for different data formats, permission models, retrieval patterns, and source-specific logic before an agent could reliably use that knowledge.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Foundry IQ simplifies this by bringing enterprise content and structured systems into a single knowledge base for multi-source, agentic retrieval. Developers can give agents access to that knowledge without building and maintaining separate connectors or source-specific retrieval strategies.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">New knowledge sources in preview:</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Work IQ</strong> brings organizational signals like emails, meetings, files, and Teams messages into one enriched, AI-ready source, all while respecting user permissions. Agents can answer questions about how the organization operates, what decisions were made, and what is top of mind for teams.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Fabric IQ</strong> lets agents query data agents and company ontologies: formal models of business entities, relationships, and rules linked to live data in OneLake and a specialized semantic layer. This returns structured answers alongside unstructured document context for a query.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>File Search</strong> allows you to directly upload files to a knowledge base.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Azure SQL</strong> brings structured relational data into a knowledge base.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>MCP Server</strong> connects knowledge served over the Model Context Protocol.</li>
</ul>



<figure class="wp-block-image"><a class="lightbox-link" href="https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/wp-content/uploads/sites/89/2026/06/build-2026-foundry-iq-01.png" target="_blank"><img decoding="async" src="https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/wp-content/uploads/sites/89/2026/06/build-2026-foundry-iq-01.png" alt="A Microsoft Foundry interface showing knowledge source selection for Foundry IQ, with options for connecting enterprise data sources into a knowledge base." /></a></figure>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Next steps: use the&nbsp;<a href="https://microsoft-foundry.github.io/forgebook/notebook/mastering-foundry-iq/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Foundry IQ Forgebook</a>&nbsp;to try out additional knowledge sources.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="microsoft-web-iq-in-foundry-iq-now-available">Microsoft Web IQ in Foundry IQ now available</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><em>When an answer needs fresh, real-world context, how do I reach the open web without paying a latency or compliance penalty?</em></p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Microsoft Web IQ is available in limited access through the Foundry IQ MCP knowledge source. It gives agents access to external retrieval across web, news, images, video, and shopping sources while honoring publisher preferences. It is designed for large language model (LLM) workflows rather than traditional search pages, with industry-leading low-latency ranking.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Combined with Foundry IQ, agents can plan, search, reason, and synthesize answers that draw on both internal knowledge and real-world external context in one retrieval engine.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Next steps: read the&nbsp;<a href="https://aka.ms/nextgengrounding" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">blog announcement</a>&nbsp;for Microsoft Web IQ.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="knowledge-bases-in-foundry-iq-are-generally-available">Knowledge bases in Foundry IQ are generally available</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><em>What does it actually take to move a prototype into production?</em></p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Production means guarantees: stable contracts, predictable performance, and security that holds under audit. Foundry IQ knowledge bases and select knowledge sources, and security capabilities are generally available: with full SLA coverage, compliance certifications, stable APIs, and enterprise-grade network isolation with identity and policy enforced by default.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">What is included in GA:</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Knowledge bases:</strong> agentic retrieval references, output and activity logs, the Foundry IQ MCP server, and minimal retrieval reasoning effort.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Foundry IQ MCP server:</strong> exposes Foundry IQ knowledge bases as a remote MCP server, making them accessible from any MCP-compatible host or client, including Claude, ChatGPT, LangChain, and the Microsoft Agent Framework. Network isolation, document-level security, cross-source ranking, and agentic retrieval all work over the open MCP standard, making it available for the broader agent ecosystem.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Knowledge sources:</strong> Azure Blob Storage (with a status API to check indexing progress), search indexes, Web, and OneLake.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Security:</strong> network isolation and managed identity support.</li>
</ul>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><em>“We’ve been using Foundry IQ in our research and prototyping work, and the reusable knowledge base approach has cut a lot of the setup overhead we’d normally expect. Being able to ground agents in trusted enterprise content from day one, without rebuilding retrieval logic each time, has made early-stage experimentation noticeably faster and higher quality.”</em>&nbsp;—&nbsp;<strong>Jane Chen</strong>, Lead AI Developer, Baringa Partners</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Next steps: use the&nbsp;<a href="https://microsoft-foundry.github.io/forgebook/notebook/mastering-foundry-iq/#11-talk-to-the-knowledge-base-directly-over-mcp" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Mastering Foundry IQ cookbook</a>&nbsp;to get started building with the Foundry IQ MCP server.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="agentic-retrieval-quality-improvements">Agentic retrieval quality improvements</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The latest retrieval enhancements improved our answer quality benchmarks by up to 20%, across our evaluated datasets, effort tiers, and model sizes. Compared to single-shot RAG, knowledge bases&nbsp;<a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-evals" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">improved recall by up to 54%</a>.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Foundry IQ improved its iterative agentic retrieval loop to batch queries more effectively, surface more relevant passages via semantic ranker, and apply server-side token caching to reduce redundant consumption across multi-turn conversations. This results in meaningfully fewer tokens spent without sacrificing answer quality, while beating previous benchmarks on answer quality.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Next steps:&nbsp;<a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-evals" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">read our blog</a>&nbsp;for more on the latest evaluations and Foundry IQ benchmarks.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="security-updates-in-preview">Security updates in preview</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><em>How do I keep enterprise data permissions intact as content flows into agents?</em></p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Security belongs at the data layer, not approximated in application code. Several security capabilities are now in preview, including cross-tenant customer-managed keys (CMK) using federated identity credentials — eliminating shared secrets — Purview sensitivity-label auditing, incremental SharePoint permissions sync, APIM support for Foundry model integrations, and surfacing Purview sensitivity labels inside knowledge sources so label-based access controls are honored end to end.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Private connectivity between Foundry IQ and Foundry products, via Shared Private Link and Network Security Perimeter, is generally available.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><em>“By integrating Foundry IQ, we provide a managed, permission-aware business context layer that connects marketing and brand knowledge into every agent so they can access the right information, at the right time, with the right governance.”</em>&nbsp;—&nbsp;<strong>Andrei Pop</strong>, Director of PM, Innovation, Sitecore</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Next steps:&nbsp;<a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-security" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">read more</a>&nbsp;about the latest Foundry IQ security announcements.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="data-pipeline-updates-in-preview">Data pipeline updates in preview</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><em>How do I make sure agents are grounded in the whole document (tables, diagrams, and images) not just the raw text?</em></p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Ingestion quality sets the ceiling on retrieval quality. New data pipeline capabilities in preview include first-class SharePoint indexing for ASPX pages and Lists alongside document libraries and document enrichment to process images plus serve them at query time in knowledge bases, so agents and users can reference original visuals and ask follow-up questions about them. We are also introducing Azure Content Understanding chunking with image verbalization — a layout-aware ingestion pipeline that converts diagrams, charts, and scanned images into meaningful text so agents are grounded in complete, semantically accurate representations of source documents.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Next steps: read Foundry IQ’s data pipeline&nbsp;<a href="https://aka.ms/FoundryIQ-data" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">deep dive blog post</a>.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="get-started-today">Get started today</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Build once, reuse everywhere: Foundry IQ enables you to ground multiple agents with the same knowledge base, connecting and unifying data from anywhere. Foundry IQ is designed for agent workloads to deliver better results from your company’s IQ. With Foundry IQ, accelerate agent delivery, deliver context without blind spots, and ensure every answer respects your organization’s security by default.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The easiest way to explore Foundry IQ is through the&nbsp;<a href="https://ai.azure.com/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft Foundry portal</a>. From there you can create a knowledge base, access the&nbsp;<a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/foundry/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">documentation</a>, and follow the&nbsp;<a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/training/paths/develop-generative-ai-apps/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft Foundry Learn courses</a>, all in a few clicks.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Be sure to check out the latest news from Foundry IQ at Microsoft Build 2026:</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item"><a href="https://build.microsoft.com/en-US/sessions/BRK246" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><strong>BRK246</strong></a>: Foundry IQ: Fuel agents with enterprise knowledge and agentic retrieval</li>

		<title>A Developer’s Guide to Managing Models, Cost and Quality in Microsoft Foundry</title>
		<link>https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/build-2026-foundry-models/</link>

		<pubDate>Tue, 02 Jun 2026 16:00:00 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[AI + machine learning]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[AI]]></category>
		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/?p=51596</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>Microsoft Foundry helps teams move beyond model access to operate AI at scale—selecting, evaluating, optimizing, and governing models across the full lifecycle.</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/build-2026-foundry-models/">A Developer’s Guide to Managing Models, Cost and Quality in Microsoft Foundry</a> appeared first on <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog">Microsoft Azure Blog</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[
<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The hardest part of building AI systems today is no longer getting access to a capable model. It is knowing how to choose, validate, optimize, and operate the right model across the full lifecycle of a real application.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Take a retrieval-augmented generation (RAG)-based customer support copilot or a tool-calling agent that helps employees complete business workflows. In a prototype, it may be enough to pick a strong model, connect a few data sources, and get a useful response. In production, the system needs to retrieve the right context, call the right tools, meet quality and safety thresholds, stay within latency targets, and run at a cost the business can sustain.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Models evolve, costs shift, and production requirements often arrive after the first version is already working. Success depends less on choosing the most powerful model and more on building a disciplined operating approach around the application.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That is where&nbsp;<a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/foundry/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft Foundry</a>&nbsp;comes in: a unified platform to select, evaluate, optimize, operate, and continuously improve AI applications at production scale.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="what’s-new">What’s new</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Microsoft Foundry continues to expand the model ecosystem and operating surface for developers building production AI systems.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IEGtTgN-Tmg" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Fireworks AI on Microsoft Foundry</a>&nbsp;is now generally available, giving developers access to production-grade open model inference through a single Azure endpoint, with enterprise service-level agreements (SLAs) and zero-setup onboarding.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Foundry is also adding new model families and capabilities across modalities, including Microsoft AI models, partner models, open-source models, custom models, and post-trained variants. Together, these updates give developers more choice while keeping selection, evaluation, deployment, and operations in one consistent workflow.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="the-challenge-is-no-longer-access.-it-is-operations.">The challenge is no longer access. It is operations.</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">In a prototype, the questions are simple: Can the model answer the prompt? Can it connect to my data? Can it complete the happy path?</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">In production, the questions change. Which model fits each task? How do I validate it on my own data? What latency budget does this experience require? How much throughput do I need at peak? What happens when quota is constrained, costs spike, or a newer model becomes available? How do I monitor quality, detect eval drift, roll back safely, and prove the system is governed?</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Agentic systems often fail when the model is mismatched, evaluation is incomplete, costs run unchecked, or governance arrives too late. Teams that rely on a single provider face another risk: lock-in, with no escape hatch when a model degrades, pricing changes, or capacity becomes constrained.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Foundry is built on the opposite philosophy. It is a model-agnostic platform spanning Microsoft, open-source, and independent software vendor (ISV) partner models, all on the same operating surface.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The answer is to treat model selection and optimization as a continuous operating discipline:<strong>&nbsp;</strong></p>



<figure class="wp-block-image"><a class="lightbox-link" href="https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/wp-content/uploads/sites/89/2026/06/model-optimization-loop.webp" target="_blank"><img decoding="async" src="https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/wp-content/uploads/sites/89/2026/06/model-optimization-loop.webp" alt="Model optimization loop showing how teams select, evaluate, optimize, operate, and improve models over time" /></a></figure>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="1.-select-the-right-model-for-the-task">1. Select the right model for the task</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Model selection is about workload fit, not leaderboard rank. Before choosing a model, define the task contract: what the model needs to do, what good looks like, what constraints it must operate within, and which failure modes are unacceptable.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">A routing step may need low latency. A policy question may need grounded reasoning with citations. A coding agent may need deeper reasoning and tool use. A customer-facing copilot may need strong safety boundaries, predictable latency, and cost efficiency at scale.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">A simple model selection framework:</p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-fixed-layout"><thead><tr><th class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Workload need</th><th class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Favor this approach</th><th class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Why</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Classification, routing, extraction, or high-volume chat</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Smaller, lower-latency model</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Keeps cost and latency low</td></tr><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Complex reasoning, coding, or planning</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Stronger reasoning model</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Improves quality for harder tasks</td></tr><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Image, speech, voice, or physical AI</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Modality-specific model</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Matches the model to the input and output type</td></tr><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Mixed workloads with different complexity</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Model Router</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Routes each request based on quality, cost, and latency</td></tr><tr><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Domain-specific behavior, tone, or format</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Fine-tuned or custom model</td><td class="has-text-align-left" data-align="left">Improves consistency for your scenario</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Effective model choice depends on four dimensions:&nbsp;<strong>capability, safety, latency, and cost.</strong></p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Foundry helps developers make these tradeoffs through a broad model ecosystem and a consistent operating surface. Developers can access Microsoft models, leading base models, partner models like Fireworks AI, open-source models, custom models, and post-trained variants through one selection, evaluation, and deployment workflow.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>Developer tip:</strong>&nbsp;For developers who want to bypass manual selection, Foundry provides Model Router in Foundry Models. Model Router automatically routes each request to the most appropriate model based on workload characteristics, cost targets, and latency requirements.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="2.-validate-with-your-own-evals-and-data">2. Validate with your own evals and data</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Benchmarks are not enough. A model that leads a public leaderboard may still underperform on your prompts, your data, your users, and your business rules. Production confidence comes from evaluating against the workloads your application will actually run.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">With Foundry, developers can bring their own evaluation inputs, including CSV or JSONL datasets with prompts, expected outputs, labels, or ground-truth answers. They can run side-by-side comparisons across models and prompts, evaluate agents and multi-step workflows, and inspect results across datasets, traces, and production-like scenarios.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Built-in quality and safety evaluators help measure signals such as relevance, groundedness, coherence, fluency, safety, and policy adherence. Custom evaluators can capture application-specific rules, formats, and business logic.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">A strong evaluation covers:</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>Quality:</strong>&nbsp;Did the model complete the task correctly?&nbsp;<strong>Accuracy and groundedness:</strong>&nbsp;Did it produce reliable answers based on the right context?&nbsp;<strong>Safety:</strong>&nbsp;Did it follow policies and avoid unacceptable responses?&nbsp;<strong>Performance:</strong>&nbsp;Did it meet latency, throughput, and reliability requirements?&nbsp;<strong>Cost:</strong>&nbsp;Did it deliver the right outcome at the right price?</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Evaluation should run continuously as new model versions, fine-tuned variants, agent changes, or new model families become available.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>Developer tip:</strong>&nbsp;Define success criteria before opening the model catalog. Criteria-first evaluation prevents anchoring on model reputation instead of workload fit.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="3.-optimize-cost-and-performance">3. Optimize cost and performance</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Cost is a first-class architectural concern, not an afterthought. In prototypes, it may be acceptable to send every task to the most capable model. In production, that approach breaks down quickly.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">A simple classification task, a RAG response, a long-context reasoning workflow, and a multi-step agentic process should not always use the same model or deployment strategy.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Foundry gives developers levers to optimize across quality, cost, and latency at the system level:</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>Intelligent routing:</strong>&nbsp;Send each task to the right model based on complexity and budget.&nbsp;<strong>Batching:</strong>&nbsp;Use asynchronous processing for workloads that do not require real-time responses.&nbsp;<strong>Caching:</strong>&nbsp;Avoid paying repeatedly for identical or near-identical requests.&nbsp;<strong>Provisioned throughput:</strong>&nbsp;Use dedicated capacity for predictable performance at scale.&nbsp;<strong>Quota management:</strong>&nbsp;Scale more predictably with quota tiering, global customer quota, and data zone customer quota.&nbsp;<strong>Model optimization:</strong>&nbsp;Use model compression, fine-tuning, or distillation where appropriate.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Fireworks AI on Foundry is now generally available, giving developers access to a high-performance open model catalog through a single Azure endpoint, with enterprise SLAs, no separate infrastructure, and no separate contracts.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>Developer tip:</strong>&nbsp;Profile cost by task type before optimizing globally. Routing decisions are workload-specific, not one-size-fits-all.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="4.-operate-at-scale-with-enterprise-confidence">4. Operate at scale with enterprise confidence</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Deploying an endpoint is not the same as operating a production AI system. Teams need to understand how the system behaves, enforce policies, monitor usage and cost, test model changes safely, and roll back when quality or performance regresses.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Foundry brings these operating capabilities into one surface: versioning, SLA-backed reliability, security, governance, access controls, audit logging, usage monitoring, and controlled upgrades.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Teams can monitor token usage and throughput, inspect logs and traces, evaluate model and agent behavior, enforce policies, and compare changes before rolling them out broadly. As new model versions become available, they can test against evaluation datasets and traces, validate quality, latency, and cost impact, and reduce risk with versioning and rollback strategies.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The Fireworks AI on Foundry generally available (GA) release is a concrete example of this operating model, with enterprise SLAs, provisioned throughput unit (PTU) Data Zone support, SOC2 readiness, and the same access controls and audit logging that govern Foundry.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Production adopters span AI-native and traditional enterprise workloads, including Perplexity, Motif, UiPath, and StackBlitz. During preview, the platform processed more than 176 billion tokens across 17 S&amp;P 500 enterprises.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>Developer tip:</strong>&nbsp;Treat model upgrades like dependency upgrades: test against baselines, stage rollouts, monitor regressions, and keep a rollback plan.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="5.-continuously-improve-as-models-and-workloads-evolve">5. Continuously improve as models and workloads evolve</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">AI systems are dynamic. Models improve, workloads shift, user behavior changes, pricing evolves, and new model families arrive. The best system today may not be the best system six months from now.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That is why the lifecycle loop matters:</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>Select</strong>&nbsp;the right model for the task.&nbsp;<strong>Evaluate</strong>&nbsp;it against your own data and production baselines.&nbsp;<strong>Optimize</strong>&nbsp;for quality, cost, latency, and throughput.&nbsp;<strong>Operate</strong>&nbsp;with governance, observability, and reliability.&nbsp;<strong>Improve</strong>&nbsp;as new models, tools, and customization options emerge.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For engineering teams, every model, prompt, tool, agent, or workflow change should be treated like a production change. New model versions should be tested automatically against regression datasets, production traces, and known edge cases before rollout.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">A model may improve quality but increase latency, reduce cost but weaken groundedness, or perform better on common cases while regressing on high-risk scenarios. Automated evaluations help teams detect those tradeoffs early.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>Developer tip:</strong>&nbsp;Automate your evaluation pipeline so every new model version is compared against production baselines for quality, safety, latency, throughput, and cost before deployment.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="what-this-means-for-developers">What this means for developers</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The next phase of AI development will not be won by teams that simply have access to the biggest models. It will be won by teams that know how to operate models well.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That means choosing by workload fit, validating with real data, optimizing cost and performance, deploying with governance, and improving as the landscape shifts.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Microsoft Foundry is designed for exactly this reality: a model-agnostic platform spanning Microsoft, open-source, and ISV models, all on one operating surface. No lock-in. No re-architecture. No guesswork.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The future of AI development is not about guessing which model might work. It is about building an operating discipline that lets you know.</p>
